    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3707008813058747491">Arthritic and immobilized, Poirot calls on his old friend Captain Hastings to join him at Styles to be the eyes and ears that will feed observations to Poirot's still razor sharp mind. Though aware of the criminal's identity, Poirot will not reveal it to the frustrated Hastings, and dubs the nameless personage 'X'. Already responsible for several murders, X, Poirot warns, </span>
  <span id="freeText3707008813058747491" style="display:none">Arthritic and immobilized, Poirot calls on his old friend Captain Hastings to join him at Styles to be the eyes and ears that will feed observations to Poirot's still razor sharp mind. Though aware of the criminal's identity, Poirot will not reveal it to the frustrated Hastings, and dubs the nameless personage 'X'. Already responsible for several murders, X, Poirot warns, is ready to strike again, and the partners must work swiftly to prevent imminent murder.<br /><br />Poirot’s final case, a mystery which brings him and Hastings back to Styles where they first solved a crime together. The story was both anticipated and dreaded by Agatha Christie fans worldwide, many of whom still refuse to read it, as it is known to contain Poirot’s death.<br /><br />Agatha Christie wrote it during World War II, as a gift for her daughter should she not survive the bombings, and it was kept in a safe for over thirty years. It was agreed among the family that Curtain would be published finally in 1975 by Collins, her long-standing publishers, and that Sleeping Murder (the Marple story written during the war for her husband, Max) would follow.<br /><br />The reception of Poirot’s death was international, even earning him an obituary in The New York Times; he is still the only fictional character to have received such an honour. The first actor to take on the role of portraying Poirot in his final hours was David Suchet, as the final episode of the series Agatha Christie’s Poirot for which he’d been playing the role for twenty-five years. The episode was adapted in 2013.</span>

      </div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">For me, it works better as the last one in the Poirot series but it would work if it's read out of order. Personally I would make sure that you read T<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">For me, it works better as the last one in the Poirot series but it would work if it's read out of order. Personally I would make sure that you read The Mysterious Affair at Styles first, as there are a few references to that case. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <span id="freeText596306747034515158" style="display:none">Curtain (Hercule Poirot Mysteries #42), Written about 1940, published 1975, Agatha Christie (1891 – 1976)<br /><br />Abstract: The crime-fighting careers of Hercule Poirot and Captain Hastings have come full circle they are back once again in the rambling country house in which they solved their first murder together. <div id="review_2004368483" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004368483" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004368483?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004368483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10436762892953611508">Rating: The Full Five<br/><br/>When this novel came out in 1975, my older sister was a bookshop owner and gave me and our mother a copy to savor. None of the three of us were particular Christie nuts. My sister felt that Dame Ags played gawd with the clues a bit too much...my mother found Poirot insufferably smug. I read the book without discrimination or comprehension, and moved on to other things I liked better. I believe that was the year I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41069.Stand_on_Zanzibar' title='Stand on Zanzibar by John Brunner' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stand on Zanzibar</a>, but am not positive.<br/><br/>Now that I'm the a</span>
  <span id="freeText10436762892953611508" style="display:none">Rating: The Full Five<br /><br />When this novel came out in 1975, my older sister was a bookshop owner and gave me and our mother a copy to savor. None of the three of us were particular Christie nuts. My sister felt that Dame Ags played gawd with the clues a bit too much...my mother found Poirot insufferably smug. I read the book without discrimination or comprehension, and moved on to other things I liked better. I believe that was the year I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41069.Stand_on_Zanzibar" title="Stand on Zanzibar by John Brunner" rel="nofollow noopener">Stand on Zanzibar</a>, but am not positive.<br /><br />Now that I'm the age my mother was when she read the book, I see something more interesting to old-man me than ever would have occurred to teenaged me. This ending for Poirot's career was written during the Blitz, a time when anyone at all could die without warning, because Dame Agatha thought her fans deserved an ending to their character's life that would give completeness and finality to an important part of a series-book reader's life. How very thoughtful that is. How aware Dame Agatha was of her creation's place in the emotional lives of her fans.<br /><br />And to her most ardent partisans, those who bristle at the probable cause of the evident diminution of her writing prowess due to dementia, I can only say: Read this book, and then read the last book she wrote, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/148584.Elephants_Can_Remember__Hercule_Poirot___37_" title="Elephants Can Remember (Hercule Poirot, #37) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Elephants Can Remember</a>, which I've reviewed unfavorably elsewhere. The difference is stark and deeply saddening.<br /><br />The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curtain_(novel)#Adaptation_for_television" rel="nofollow noopener">2013 television adaptation</a> is stellar and gets, on its own merits, a five-star review. David Suchet so completely became Poirot that I can only hope someone somewhere possesses both the power and the will to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murder_on_the_Orient_Express_(2017_film)" rel="nofollow noopener">derail the 2017 adaptation</a> of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16304.Murder_on_the_Orient_Express__Hercule_Poirot___10_" title="Murder on the Orient Express (Hercule Poirot, #10) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Murder on the Orient Express</a> perpetrated by Kenneth Branagh for no good or even comprehensible reason before its scheduled release on 10 November 2017. Why not choose 11/11/17 at 11:11am? Armistice Day might, in the eyes of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calliope" rel="nofollow noopener">Kalliope</a>, excuse or at least obscure Branagh's hubris in making this unneeded and unwelcome film.<br /><br />Not that I have a strong opinion, you understand. I merely comment upon the passing scene, comme d'habitude.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10436762892953611508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3445858482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3445858482" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3445858482?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=crime-and-mystery">crime-and-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=hercule-poirot">hercule-poirot</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3445858482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8876242793482847342">Poirot's last novel and last case. Things came full circle and Captain Hastings went to Styles where he had seen a Poirot's investigation for the first time. Only now Poirot was crippled and lost use of his legs, but the gray cells... the gray cells still worked. Hastings had no clue that Poirot was about to match his wits with a genius serial killer who could never be accused of his crimes by any court, or even suspected - sort of like Professor Moriarty if you will, but their methods were very</span>
  <span id="freeText8876242793482847342" style="display:none">Poirot's last novel and last case. Things came full circle and Captain Hastings went to Styles where he had seen a Poirot's investigation for the first time. Only now Poirot was crippled and lost use of his legs, but the gray cells... the gray cells still worked. Hastings had no clue that Poirot was about to match his wits with a genius serial killer who could never be accused of his crimes by any court, or even suspected - sort of like Professor Moriarty if you will, but their methods were very different. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595811591i/29864232.jpg" alt="Moriarty" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let me start with the things I did not like and even hated sometimes. Hastings' IQ lowered since the first book and he was not exactly Einstein to begin with. Poirot's constant gloating about the fact got on my nerves - after all, Hastings could not help being stupid and he had to be pitied, not constantly being reminded about. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595811759i/29864238._SX540_.jpg" alt="Forrest Gump" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Personally, oh my God mercifully he was not present in the large part of the series, especially in the later books and I forgot about his low mental abilities. Here I was for a rude reawakening to the fact. <br><br>Having said that, his daughter was present in the action. I regret to say she took her mental abilities from her father and I also suspect she was dropped on her head repeatedly when she was a toddler. She was shown as a capable biologist, but in ordinary situations she made her father look like a genius. I am not talking here about the eccentricity and lack of attention of some talented people, I am talking about stupidity (in other words, she was mentally challenged to put in into modern terms). It did not help any that she behaved like a young rebellious teen - and I have it on good authority that not all of them are <i>that</i> bad.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595811935i/29864242._SX540_.jpg" alt="Teen Rebellion" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The villain was painfully obvious from relatively early in the book for any reader who satisfies the following two conditions. First, he or she (or it) needs to have an IQ slightly higher than Captain Hastings (and much higher than his daughter). Second, a will to exercise the aforementioned gray cells - just a little, mind you. So do not expect usual crazily complicated plot which is a trademark by the Queen of Mystery. <br><br>I did not like the way she treated Poirot. I totally understand by the time of writing she was tired of the character and publishers and readers still demanded more of his adventures. Sure the guy had an ego of the size of a modern aircraft carrier, <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595811480i/29864230._SX540_.jpg" alt="Carrier" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>but I like his conviction that murder is wrong - and he always kept it and he never let his ego get in the way of it. <br><br>Lastly this book was written <i>before</i> the previous one of the series and it feels less modern than the letter - this was a little jarring. But here I am nitpicking. <br><br>So from what I wrote about one would think that the rating is 3 stars, but I gave 4. There are three reasons. My general respect for the whole series and the character of Poirot. The villain who was very good and interesting (and very villainous). Also after all I said it is still a great farewell to the second greatest private detective of the literature. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8876242793482847342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2202080619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2202080619" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2202080619?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=mystery-detective-thriller">mystery-detective-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=christie">christie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2202080619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7796712924209358026">Curtain: Poirot’s Last Case!<br/><br/>“Nothing is so sad, in my opinion, as the devastation wrought by age”—Hastings, on Poirot<br/><br/>I’m done, whew, having read all of 38 Christie Poirot novels (and a couple short story collections) in order of publication, over the past 2-3 years. I’ll listen again to And Then There Were None and will not read Christie again for awhile, I am sure.<br/><br/>Christie, fearing for her life during WWII, wrote the last Poirot and Marple books in the early forties, and sealed them in a vault </span>
  <span id="freeText7796712924209358026" style="display:none">Curtain: Poirot’s Last Case!<br /><br />“Nothing is so sad, in my opinion, as the devastation wrought by age”—Hastings, on Poirot<br /><br />I’m done, whew, having read all of 38 Christie Poirot novels (and a couple short story collections) in order of publication, over the past 2-3 years. I’ll listen again to And Then There Were None and will not read Christie again for awhile, I am sure.<br /><br />Christie, fearing for her life during WWII, wrote the last Poirot and Marple books in the early forties, and sealed them in a vault until just a couple years before her death, intending them to be the last novels, the last word, for her respective detective heroes. She much preferred Marple to Poirot, who in the sixties she had truly grown tired of, calling him "an egocentric creep". However, unlike Conan Doyle, Christie resisted the temptation to kill her detective off while he was still popular. She saw herself as an entertainer whose job was to produce what the public liked, and the public liked Poirot. <br /><br />Christie made a mistake in 1920 in having her Belgian detective already retired, afterwards writing him as a main character for fifty more years!! So are we to surmise he retired at 40? 21?! Poirot returns to Styles in this one, where the first Poirot novel is set, written in 1920 when Christie was 30. Curtain was published in 1975, less than a year before she died, at 85, in 1976!! 55 years of writing Poirot!! Poor (and very rich) woman! Good for her and us, though, on the whole, as she emerged as the best selling author of all time.<br /><br />And no matter how old he is, we need our main man with the marvelous moustaches to be in full possession of his “little gray cells” right up until the end. Is this realistic? Well, either way he seems undiminished in speech and cognition without fail. The erosion of memory is a theme in this and many of the last books for the eighty-something Christie, but not for Poirot! He solves the crime, as always, though it is complicated and interesting how it happens and how it is revealed; I can’t exactly say how without spoilers.<br /><br />This book also features the early Poirot-books Captain Hastings, a buffoon who again tells the story, clueless every step of the way. <br /><br />Keyholes figure in, amusingly.<br /><br />Since Curtain is the title, Christie frames her last book in terms of her major love, theater, and performance, and disguises. We even discover Poirot has been disguising himself for years, in a way. And Othello’s Iago figures in, so Shakespeare is her darling right to the end for inspiration. <br /><br />This may not be one of the very best of his books, but it is clever, with better writing than we have seen for many years from Christie (because she wrote it in the forties!). She also doesn’t bother to pull it from the vault to revise it for continuity, grr. For instance, the supposedly older Poirot here has more problems with colloquial English than he has had in decades, consistent with a forties Poirot, not a seventies Poirot. But overall, it was good to bring back Hastings, and to end as we began, in Styles. And the killer—a serial killer—and how he kills, is original and interesting. It is a very good book in the Christie canon and because of the nature of the killer and because of the series of Big Surprises in the plot, I am going to bump it from 4.5 to 5 stars.<br /><br />A SPOILER ALERT about something very sweet that had never before happened, hidden in this link to the historically stuffy The New York Times, 6 August 1975, following the publication of Curtain.:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nytimes.com/1975/08/06/archives/hercule-poirot-is-dead-famed-belgian-detective-hercule-poirot-the.html">http://www.nytimes.com/1975/08/06/arc...</a><br /><br />My five star Poirots:<br /><br />The Murder of Roger Ackroyd<br />Peril at End House<br />Murder on the Orient Express<br />Curtain<br /><br />My four star Poirots:<br /><br />Lord Edgeware Dies<br />Three Act Tragedy<br />The A.B.C. Murders<br />Murder in Mesopotamia<br />Cards on the Table<br />Death on the Nile<br />Sad Cypress<br />Evil Under the Sun<br />Five Little Pig<br />The Hollow<br />After the Funeral</span>
  <a data-text-id="7796712924209358026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1379958225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1379958225" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1379958225?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780002316194" href="/book/show/519243.Curtain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1379958225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15577987311177775022">Agatha Christie's swan song for her most famous character, Hercule Poirot, fittingly returns him and and his friend Arthur Hastings to the setting of her very first novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16343.The_Mysterious_Affair_at_Styles__Hercule_Poirot___1_' title='The Mysterious Affair at Styles (Hercule Poirot, #1) by Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Mysterious Affair at Styles</a>. Aside from the fact that it's Poirot's final case, a rather unusual twist and the recurring <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12996.Othello' title='Othello by William Shakespeare' rel='nofollow noopener'>Othello</a> theme make this one of Christie's more memorable works, if rather melancholy. <br/><br/>It was interesting to find out that Christie originally wrote this novel during World War II, possibly fearing that s</span>
  <span id="freeText15577987311177775022" style="display:none">Agatha Christie's swan song for her most famous character, Hercule Poirot, fittingly returns him and and his friend Arthur Hastings to the setting of her very first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16343.The_Mysterious_Affair_at_Styles__Hercule_Poirot___1_" title="The Mysterious Affair at Styles (Hercule Poirot, #1) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mysterious Affair at Styles</a>. Aside from the fact that it's Poirot's final case, a rather unusual twist and the recurring <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12996.Othello" title="Othello by William Shakespeare" rel="nofollow noopener">Othello</a> theme make this one of Christie's more memorable works, if rather melancholy. <br /><br />It was interesting to find out that Christie originally wrote this novel during World War II, possibly fearing that she might not survive the war and wanting to give Poirot an appropriate send-off. Then she put <i>Curtain</i> in a bank vault for over 30 years, finally publishing it in 1975. It was her last published book before she died.<br /><br /><i>Au revoir</i>, Agatha and Hercule.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15577987311177775022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1379958225">

<span id="freeTextContainer14057374204788722773"><i>"For a murderer, my friend, is more conceited than any creature on this earth. A murderer is always more clever than anyone else- no one will ever suspect him or her- the police will be utterly baffled"</i><br/><br/>The above quote is a perfect way to describe this mystery.<br/><br/>I have been wanting to read this for some time now and what better day than Christie's birthday.<br/><br/>I have now read numerous mysteries by Christie but there is no pattern (apart from a cozy setting)<br/>Each and every mystery, murder suspects, the e</span>
  <span id="freeText14057374204788722773" style="display:none"><i>"For a murderer, my friend, is more conceited than any creature on this earth. A murderer is always more clever than anyone else- no one will ever suspect him or her- the police will be utterly baffled"</i><br><br>The above quote is a perfect way to describe this mystery.<br><br>I have been wanting to read this for some time now and what better day than Christie's birthday.<br><br>I have now read numerous mysteries by Christie but there is no pattern (apart from a cozy setting)<br>Each and every mystery, murder suspects, the end is unique and it baffles me as generally when you read many books by one author some things do become predictable.<br><br><b>The only thing I have learnt after reading Agatha Christie books is that expect the unexpected and still you won't guess how shocking the unexpected can be!</b><br><br><b>This is the last in the series of Poirot mysteries and I would recommend to read the first of this series- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16343.The_Mysterious_Affair_at_Styles__Hercule_Poirot___1_" title="The Mysterious Affair at Styles (Hercule Poirot, #1) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mysterious Affair at Styles</a> before this as both the mysteries take place at Styles and there is a spoiler to the first book in this story.</b><br><i>"And suddenly from nowhere, a vague feeling of uneasiness and disquiet assailed me. It was not safe- it was not right- to plan happiness here. There was something malignant about the air of Styles"</i><br><br>Poirot and Hastings come together in this last case together to catch X who is clever and sadistic as any murderer can be. There is a mix of lovely characters who make you trust them but doubt them at the same time.<br><i>"Everyone is a potential murderer- in everyone there arises from time to time the wish to kill- though not the will to kill"</i><br><br><b>The ending is soo ingenious but soo complicated, I just had to sit back and digest it all</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474135127ra/20559782.gif" height="" width="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>There is no way I could have guessed this. Did you?</b></span>

<div id="review_109320246" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109320246" />
    <a title="Laurel Young" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3137295-laurel-young"><img alt="Laurel Young" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500435810p2/3137295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109320246?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurel Young" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurel Young" href="/user/show/3137295-laurel-young">Laurel Young</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3137295-laurel-young?shelf=my-year-of-agatha">my-year-of-agatha</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109320246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12577322890483720973">I admit it, I teared up at the end; I don't ever want there to be a final Poirot novel. However, two things comforted me: one is that this was not actually the last novel Dame Agatha wrote about Poirot, not by a long shot. Since Elephants Can Remember is largely regarded as a weak later effort, I think of Hallowe'en Party as the last excellent novel written about Poirot. Curtain was written somewhere around WWII most likely, and put away to be released decades later as Agatha neared the end of h</span>
  <span id="freeText12577322890483720973" style="display:none">I admit it, I teared up at the end; I don't ever want there to be a final Poirot novel. However, two things comforted me: one is that this was not actually the last novel Dame Agatha wrote about Poirot, not by a long shot. Since Elephants Can Remember is largely regarded as a weak later effort, I think of Hallowe'en Party as the last excellent novel written about Poirot. Curtain was written somewhere around WWII most likely, and put away to be released decades later as Agatha neared the end of her long career. So it is always possible to read the novels in chronological order and pretend that Poirot is back for all his many post-WWII cases, rather like Sherlock Holmes' return from "The Final Problem". <br /><br />But the biggest comfort is that this truly excellent novel could not have been written without <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ killing off Poirot--it is in some ways the ultimate twist from the author famous for brilliant, unexpected twists. Agatha often expressed the idea that ANYONE is capable of murder in the right circumstances, and her novels show that the last person the reader expects to have done it, could have done it--the narrator, a child, a supposedly dead character, etc! In Curtain, Agatha hits us with the biggest shocker of them all: even her Great Detective is not immune. Poirot can and does commit murder, and even "mon ami Hastings" makes a (typically blundering!) attempt...and both are completely in character whilst doing so. No doubt Agatha wanted to write the detective author's White Whale: the perfect crime. And who could pull off the perfect crime except Poirot himself??  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There are many satisfying elements in this novel to console the bereaved reader. There is the perfect symmetry of having Poirot's English career end where it began, at Styles Court (and many other, more minor symmetries along the way). There is the character development of Hastings, shown here as far more complex that one usually credits him as being, and given hope of a happy ending and a new romance thoughtfully provided by Poirot! There is the delightful surprise that, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ far from being the cripple Hastings thinks him to be, Poirot remains agile and able to sleuth until the very end. His grey cells are in fine fettle until his dying day.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Curtain is supremely clever and confident, one of Dame Agatha's tours de force. I am glad, though, that she never <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ killed off Miss Marple.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I really don't think I could handle that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12577322890483720973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2927626362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2927626362" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/100387236-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567614515p2/100387236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2927626362?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/100387236-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2927626362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9443744618717802302">I am sad that I had to give 2 stars to an Agatha Christie book because I am a huge fan. I took this book with a lot of hope. This book is so famous I thought I will have a fantastic reading experience with it. I felt distraught after reading it. <br/><br/>The 2 stars are for the following:<br/><br/>The original idea of the story, a criminal who puts thoughts into people and make them commit crimes. It was brilliant. Totally awesome.<br/><br/>Secondly, the book portrays many kinds of people and their relationships. And I thou</span>
  <span id="freeText9443744618717802302" style="display:none">I am sad that I had to give 2 stars to an Agatha Christie book because I am a huge fan. I took this book with a lot of hope. This book is so famous I thought I will have a fantastic reading experience with it. I felt distraught after reading it. <br /><br />The 2 stars are for the following:<br /><br />The original idea of the story, a criminal who puts thoughts into people and make them commit crimes. It was brilliant. Totally awesome.<br /><br />Secondly, the book portrays many kinds of people and their relationships. And I thought Christie was able to bring justice to that.<br /><br />Things I hated about this book:<br /><br />Characters: Apparently the only character I could like was that of the murderer.( sigh!) All the rest of them were totally unbearable. Couldn't stand anyone including Poirot. I couldn't accept their opinions. I hated Poirot for constantly mocking Hastings who is mind you his closest friend and has come to visit Poirot because he asked for him. Now if I were Hastings, I would have left Poirot to succumb to his ailments, the way he treated me. Its almost close to abuse. This is the book where I truly hated Poirot. Ok enough with this stuff.<br /><br />Plot: Oh boy. Even though the story line and relationship between the characters are greatly written, the whole story is really stupid. Like Poirot must be held responsible for atleast one murder and another attempt at murder. He could have prevented that from happening. Instead of that he just sits back in his chair and relaxes, leaving poor clueless Hastings to figure out who the murderer is, from a bunch of obnoxious, dark people. <br /><br />Conclusion: Equally terrible. Has any of the readers thought about the fact that if Poirot ( trying to avoid spoilers here, please bear with me) did what he did at the end of the story, at the beginning, everything would have been set right. Instead he waits idly so that Christie has a novel to write about!<br /><br />Really! This is probably one of the few Christie novels in which I feel Christie was trying to mock at the intellect of the reader as well as that of Hastings! (Obviously).</span>
  <a data-text-id="9443744618717802302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2998483571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2998483571" />
    <a title="Anna Luce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9429655-anna-luce"><img alt="Anna Luce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604227738p2/9429655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2998483571?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Luce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Luce" href="/user/show/9429655-anna-luce">Anna Luce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062229632" href="/book/show/15820270-curtain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=audiobooks-i-own">audiobooks-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=4-favourites">4-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=poignant-reads">poignant-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=my-feelings">my-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=3-loved-it">3-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=favourite-friendships">favourite-friendships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=2019-reviews">2019-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2998483571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12902392566546119525">★★★★✰ 4.5 stars<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Who is there who has not felt a sudden startled pang at reliving an old experience, or feeling an old emotion?”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/81903.Curtain__Hercule_Poirot___42_' title='Curtain (Hercule Poirot, #42) by Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Curtain</a> <b>bids a bittersweet farewell to the one and only Hercule Poirot</b>. While I know that by this point Agatha Christie feelings towards him were<i> less </i> than amicable, her novel doesn't convey its creators impatience. Rather than hurrying Poirot off from the stage,<b> Christie grants him one final performance</b>.<br/>I will admit that seeing <b>the formidable Poirot altered in such</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12902392566546119525" style="display:none">★★★★✰ 4.5 stars<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Who is there who has not felt a sudden startled pang at reliving an old experience, or feeling an old emotion?”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/81903.Curtain__Hercule_Poirot___42_" title="Curtain (Hercule Poirot, #42) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Curtain</a> <b>bids a bittersweet farewell to the one and only Hercule Poirot</b>. While I know that by this point Agatha Christie feelings towards him were<i> less </i> than amicable, her novel doesn't convey its creators impatience. Rather than hurrying Poirot off from the stage,<b> Christie grants him one final performance</b>.<br />I will admit that seeing <b>the formidable Poirot altered in such a visible way</b> did indeed affect me. Still, in spite of his physical appearance, his mind remains as sharp as ever and he is, as per usual, always a mile ahead of his<b> naïve friend Hastings </b>(who is yet again played like a fiddle). Surprisingly Hastings was not as irritating as he could usually be, and while his younger self was more of a stick-in-the-mud kind of chap (at times acting like little more than disgruntled child), this older Hastings seems far more genial. Hastings' feelings mirrored my own ones: <b>being at Styles again brings about a bout of nostalgia</b>, and his reunion with Poirot reveals that underneath his somewhat priggish British exterior, lies a<b> deep affection for his Belgian friend</b>. <br />Their banter was as amusing as ever, especially in those occasions when Poirot teases Hastings about his partiality for redheads.<br /> <br />While many of Christie's murderers are often motived by financial gain, in <i>Curtain</i> our '<i>X</i>' is <b>driven by much more fiendish impulse</b>s. Suspecting this, Poirot is forced to act fast. Sadly, his failing health does <i>seem </i>to disrupt his investigation so much so that Poirot finds himself seeking once again Hastings' assistance.<br />The group of people residing in Styles offer us with <b>interesting little portraits of human nature</b>: a domineering spouse, an ambitious doctor, a womaniser...some of these have indeed in some form or other in previous works by Christie but that doesn't make them any less interesting. Christie, as per usual, demonstrates that she is <b>perfectly attuned to capture certain personalities</b>—their attitudes, moral and political standpoints, as well as their fears and desires, their strengths and weaknesses—and the way in which they talk—through different word choices, expressions, and turns of phrases—so that <b>each character leaves a vivid impression in the readers' mind</b>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“As my taxi passed through the village, though, I realised the passage of years. Styles St Mary was altered out of all recognition. Petrol stations, a cinema, two more inns and rows of council houses.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Christie's own nostalgia is apparent in this novel, and Hastings, similarly to his creator, <b>perceives the changes in his world with an uneasy acceptance</b>. There are quite a few works by Christie that express <b>uncertainty over the modernisation and rapidly changing social norms of her country</b>, and these feelings particularly suited the story of <i>Curtain</i> as much of it seems to be <b>a dialogue between the various cases that have shaped Poirot's career</b>.<br />The mystery was <b>skillfully executed</b>, and I enjoyed reading of the way in which seemingly small events and exchanges seemed to alienate the characters from one another. The reveal was both <b>clever and effective</b>, bringing light to the whole affair.<br />I thoroughly recommend this one to fans of Poirot. Sad as it may be, it demonstrates<b> Christie's greatest strengths (<i>wit, murder, drama</i>)</b>. And while the novel <i>might</i> be presenting us with Poirot's final case, I am eager to be reunited with him in his early adventures...<br /><br /><a href="https://wishfullyreading.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Read more reviews on my blog</a> / / / <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/9429655-anna-luce" rel="nofollow noopener">View all my reviews on Goodreads</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12902392566546119525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/213202484" />
    <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma"><img alt="Nandakishore Varma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583648733p2/6237864.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nandakishore Varma" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780002316194" href="/book/show/519243.Curtain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6237864-nandakishore-varma?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213202484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15238781912879897226">It would be wrong to say I loved this book (despite the 5 stars)... I hated it. I love Poirot so much that I couldn't bear to see him pass beyond the veil.<br/><br/>That said, I consider this one a fantastic mystery - and one which could be resolved only this way, with the death of the detective (read the book, and you'll get what I mean). Many people have complained that the premise is far-fetched, but IMO, that is its main charm. And let me tell you, it's not all that impossible... <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[There </span></span>
  <span id="freeText15238781912879897226" style="display:none">It would be wrong to say I loved this book (despite the 5 stars)... I hated it. I love Poirot so much that I couldn't bear to see him pass beyond the veil.<br /><br />That said, I consider this one a fantastic mystery - and one which could be resolved only this way, with the death of the detective (read the book, and you'll get what I mean). Many people have complained that the premise is far-fetched, but IMO, that is its main charm. And let me tell you, it's not all that impossible... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There was a person in our family, an unmarried great aunt, who has caused at least one divorce and a prolonged estrangement between brother and sister, through subtle psychological suggestions, just for the heck of it. After this novel came out, we called her "Lady Norton"! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />BTW, Christie had written this long back and kept it with her lawyer with instructions to publish it only after her death. Poirot got an official obituary in the paper once this book was published.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2218945240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13303909685159992036">In his last case Poirot returns to where it all began for the reader, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2205081535?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Styles</a>. Here an old and physically ailing Poirot tries to track down his greatest challenge adversary: a murder who appears completely unconnected with a string of murders. A villain so devious his very existence is unknown to all but Poirot's little grey cells. As with <i>The Mysterious Affair at Styles</i> Poirot enlists the help of Hastings in tracking down the villain and it is from Hastings point of view we get the story.<br/><br/>As per </span>
  <span id="freeText13303909685159992036" style="display:none">In his last case Poirot returns to where it all began for the reader, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2205081535?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Styles</a>. Here an old and physically ailing Poirot tries to track down his greatest challenge adversary: a murder who appears completely unconnected with a string of murders. A villain so devious his very existence is unknown to all but Poirot's little grey cells. As with <i>The Mysterious Affair at Styles</i> Poirot enlists the help of Hastings in tracking down the villain and it is from Hastings point of view we get the story.<br /><br />As per usual Christie does a marvelous job both constructing the mystery and giving the characters in her story wonderful depth. Instead of merely being pieces to the mystery puzzle they all came off as independent, self-realized characters with their own agendas, hopes, and aspirations. The only part of the book that felt off to me was just how amazing the villain was at carrying out his/her craft. It was a bit too far fetched in my opinion how deft a manipulator they were, but that is really the only bad mark against this book. It was yet another top notch Christie mystery and would be enjoyed by any mystery fan.<br /><br />And Hugh Fraser is, once again, stellar as the narrator.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13303909685159992036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11723419223261563475">With apologies to all the Agatha Christie fans of the world, I simply could not get myself interested enough in this book to finish it. I tried, I really did, because my mother gave me her paperback copy after she heard that I had read the first Poirot novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16343.The_Mysterious_Affair_at_Styles__Hercule_Poirot___1_' title='The Mysterious Affair at Styles (Hercule Poirot, #1) by Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Mysterious Affair at Styles</a> . She said that since I had read the first one featuring the Belgian detective, I should also read the final one. Although I had decided not to read any other Christie titles, I gave in and took the book. How</span>
  <span id="freeText11723419223261563475" style="display:none">With apologies to all the Agatha Christie fans of the world, I simply could not get myself interested enough in this book to finish it. I tried, I really did, because my mother gave me her paperback copy after she heard that I had read the first Poirot novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16343.The_Mysterious_Affair_at_Styles__Hercule_Poirot___1_" title="The Mysterious Affair at Styles (Hercule Poirot, #1) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mysterious Affair at Styles</a> . She said that since I had read the first one featuring the Belgian detective, I should also read the final one. Although I had decided not to read any other Christie titles, I gave in and took the book. How could I say no to my 86 year-old mother?<br /><br />But I had to give up after reading the first couple of chapters and skimming a few more. I was bored; I did not feel like subjecting myself to more ramblings by Hastings, and I honestly don't care who the mysterious murderer is. This time for sure, no more Christie for me. Sorry Mom, this was a DNF. </span>

<div id="review_1144606100" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1144606100" />
    <a title="Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37868613-sophie-narey-bookreview--aholic"><img alt="Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532961691p2/37868613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144606100?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) " href="/user/show/37868613-sophie-narey-bookreview--aholic">Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of murder mystery </span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144606100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8493909467262074041">Author: Agatha Christie<br/>Published: 01/09/2000 (first published 1973)<br/><br/>Another great book by Agatha Christie! Poirot is my favourite out of the Agatha Christie books, it is sad that the Hercule Poirot series came to an end but this was a really brilliant ending. I think that this book was brilliantly and expertly written, it gripped my attention and refused to let it go, even after I finished the book my head was still rushing through how Agatha Christie can write such an amazing book. Once again wh</span>
  <span id="freeText8493909467262074041" style="display:none">Author: Agatha Christie<br />Published: 01/09/2000 (first published 1973)<br /><br />Another great book by Agatha Christie! Poirot is my favourite out of the Agatha Christie books, it is sad that the Hercule Poirot series came to an end but this was a really brilliant ending. I think that this book was brilliantly and expertly written, it gripped my attention and refused to let it go, even after I finished the book my head was still rushing through how Agatha Christie can write such an amazing book. Once again while reading this book I could never have guessed the ending. <br /> The characters and the background/setting painted a vivid picture in the readers mind, and let you really get to know all of the characters. It is sad that the series ended but I shall always enjoy reading through all of the books time after time they will never get old or boring. I love these novels! Each of the characters add something too the novel, even if they seem like background characters at the end they normally have one of the biggest parts in the mytsery, this is one of the things that I love about these books, nothing that Agatha Christie writes about in the novel is just for the sake of it, it all gets tied up together nicely at the end. <br /> I was both happy and sad to read this book, happy because it is Hercule Poirot and sad because it is the last one in the series, however it is definately the kind of book that you can read over and over again, it is a timeless classic (in my view). I would say that this book is suitable for young adults on wards as even though it is a murder mystery book the murders aren't in too much horrible detail where it would give you nightmares which makes it an interesting read that keeps your mind wondering who it is and keeps you focused on the characters and the setting.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91112987?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarai" href="/user/show/2506057-sarai">Sarai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2506057-sarai?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2506057-sarai?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91112987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer577538514454752522">Poirot is my favorite Agatha Christie sleuth. I also love the corresponding A&E Poirot series with David Suchet playing the famous Belgian detective (those moustaches!). I have to admit, I have a bit of a crush on the Poirot character. He's so smart, so wonderfully pompous but gentlemanly, a wee bit delicate, slightly neurotic, a loyal friend, and dedicated protector of the innocent. I always enjoy Poirot and Hastings working together and Poirot's gentle chiding of Hastings' deductions.<br/><br/>I conside</span>
  <span id="freeText577538514454752522" style="display:none">Poirot is my favorite Agatha Christie sleuth. I also love the corresponding A&amp;E Poirot series with David Suchet playing the famous Belgian detective (those moustaches!). I have to admit, I have a bit of a crush on the Poirot character. He's so smart, so wonderfully pompous but gentlemanly, a wee bit delicate, slightly neurotic, a loyal friend, and dedicated protector of the innocent. I always enjoy Poirot and Hastings working together and Poirot's gentle chiding of Hastings' deductions.<br /><br />I consider Christie's books to be fast, light reading.<br /><br /><br />from Amazon: By Antoinette Klein<br />"Nothing is so sad, in my opinion," muses Captain Hastings, "as the devastation wrought by age." In this final outing for the inimitable Hercule Poirot and his loyal friend Arthur Hastings, the body may be weak but Poirot's brain is still functioning magnificently. A murder will be committed, the famous detective tells his friend, and Hastings must function as Poirot's legs. Aging and failing in health, the once energetic Poirot is now confined to a wheelchair. However, that does not stop the two friends from once again going on the hunt together in a case Poirot himself tells Hastings will be his last case but his most interesting one. As a special bonus for Poirot fans, we return once again to Styles, the scene of Poirot's first adventure. A near-death of one woman followed by the actual death of another, a sadist who is able to convince others to murder, a most surprising act by Hastings himself, a peep through a keyhole, a visit to a faithful valet, and murder most symmetrical are clues that lead to the uncovering of the criminal Poirot has come to Styles to unmask. Surely, this must rank as one of Christie's finest as we bid a fond adieu to Hercule Poirot.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2675423485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2675423485" />
    <a title="Armand" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45716474-armand"><img alt="Armand" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591576251p2/45716474.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2675423485?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Armand" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Armand" href="/user/show/45716474-armand">Armand</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007121120" href="/book/show/556113.Curtain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45716474-armand?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45716474-armand?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2675423485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11434630082560110938">In the winter of his life, Hercule Poirot meets a nemesis tougher than any he's ever encountered. He knows about the chaos this criminal has left in his/her wake, and in a fateful turn of events, he ended up hounding his quarry in the very place where, as a young man, his adventures all began - Styles Court. Because yes, he knows the identity of the criminal, while like his friend Hastings we're left in the dark until the very end. This book is unique in that his goal is not to deduce whodunit, </span>
  <span id="freeText11434630082560110938" style="display:none">In the winter of his life, Hercule Poirot meets a nemesis tougher than any he's ever encountered. He knows about the chaos this criminal has left in his/her wake, and in a fateful turn of events, he ended up hounding his quarry in the very place where, as a young man, his adventures all began - Styles Court. Because yes, he knows the identity of the criminal, while like his friend Hastings we're left in the dark until the very end. This book is unique in that his goal is not to deduce whodunit, but how to catch that person in the act. This one is a particularly slippery viper, and the MO employed is one of the most ingenious I've come across in mystery books.<br /><br />And what a magnificent finish it was. It will leave you shocked, because the denouement was entirely unexpected. To defang a snake with a nearly-flawless MO, Poirot shall pay a terrible price.<br /><br />What I liked about this novel is how it proved that Poirot's honor is beyond reproach. He may be arrogant and supercilious, but one thing he never was is a hypocrite. He has integrity in spades, he's steadfast about his principles, and he's willing to defend these, using extreme means if necessary.<br /><br />I have read a lot of Christies, but this surely ranks in the top 5. It's a bravura performance, a fitting farewell to our good detective. 9.5/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="11434630082560110938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6818431207413820349">The first time we meet Poirot, he is at Styles St. Mary during World War 1. That is where Hastings first pairs up with Poirot. Many years later, they meet again at the same location. This latter meeting is the where Curtain takes place. Poirot is old physically, but still sharp mentally.   <span id="freeText6818431207413820349" style="display:none">The first time we meet Poirot, he is at Styles St. Mary during World War 1. That is where Hastings first pairs up with Poirot. Many years later, they meet again at the same location. This latter meeting is the where Curtain takes place. Poirot is old physically, but still sharp mentally. Hastings is mourning the death of his wife and worrying about his daughter, Judith, who is also visiting at the same house as her father.<br /><br />Poirot has discovered that a series of deaths seem to be connected. One person knows all of the victims and their families. Poirot thinks that this is no coincidence. So begins the final Poirot story. <br /><br />Make sure you read The Mysterious Affair at Styles first in order to appreciate both mysteries, as well as to get the feel of the changes that take place over 20-30 years in England.</span>

<div id="review_2004016087" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004016087" />
    <a title="Karin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20048682-karin"><img alt="Karin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588016778p2/20048682.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004016087?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karin" href="/user/show/20048682-karin">Karin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=1970s">1970s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=20th-century-fiction">20th-century-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=british-author">british-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=british-authors">british-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=classic">classic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004016087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4850562092383799965">Captain Arthur Hastings had been asked to join is very old friend, Hercules Poirot, at the site of the first murder Hastings saw Poirot solve. In addition, Hastings' favourite daughter, Julia, will be there. Poirot mystifies Hastings by telling him that someone he will only refer to as X is there, and that he has murdered five times before. Hastings is to try and find out who the intended victim is to try and stop the murder before it happens, but Hastings is flummoxed at the task.<br/><br/>This novel has</span>
  <span id="freeText4850562092383799965" style="display:none">Captain Arthur Hastings had been asked to join is very old friend, Hercules Poirot, at the site of the first murder Hastings saw Poirot solve. In addition, Hastings' favourite daughter, Julia, will be there. Poirot mystifies Hastings by telling him that someone he will only refer to as X is there, and that he has murdered five times before. Hastings is to try and find out who the intended victim is to try and stop the murder before it happens, but Hastings is flummoxed at the task.<br /><br />This novel has my favourite twist of all of Christie's mysteries that I've read; I'm not even sure how many that is because I can't remember most of the titles I read while in high school, but I've read a fair number. Poirot mysteries were the ones on my parents' shelves; I learned about Miss Marple much later. What's the twist? Avoid all spoilers and read the book yourself. If you can't help but read the ending before you're done, get it on audio so you can't see ahead; this book will be well worth the wait.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4850562092383799965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2605686147" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2605686147" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1881113-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537392299p2/1881113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2605686147?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/1881113-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062074096" href="/book/show/10439056-curtain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1881113-andrea?shelf=fiction-mystery">fiction-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1881113-andrea?shelf=read-sorted">read-sorted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1881113-andrea?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1881113-andrea?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2605686147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer600661301685820437">A bittersweet moment for me. My last Hercule Poirot novel and the one that takes the reader full circle to the infamous Styles, where it all began. Hastings is back too, and so the stage is set for the dazzling exit of the aging detective. It was good to go down the memory lane, to give it one more whirl in a new murder case, and to bid farewell. I shed a little tear and go back in time to when another brilliant sleuth was born - it’s time to move on to Miss Marple.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('owB/yJ/JSewdHzNXM9pBVRSJKaWdZJdi7isg8rjEwPGefaOqv8NluI/6r/gpK0ecs1fYtUlRVLQ6qQhbbeKP5A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vB8DMpf0iKB9lIpnPq6QKMdjYZCm2vWNK5HCmE6EFjKBYt9Qt/6k9O9xFsgkX5bhYL2QgHLvNlv/E+oxm6JZJw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Her name is Sylvia Rule, and she demands to know why Poirot has accused her of the murder of Barnabas Pandy, a man she has neither heard of nor ever met. She is furious to be so accused, and deeply shocked. Poirot is equally shocked, because he too has never heard of any Barnabas Pandy, and he certainly did not send the letter in question. He cannot convince Sylvia Rule of his innocence, however, and she marches away in a rage.\n\nShaken, Poirot goes inside, only to find that he has a visitor waiting for him -- a man called John McCrodden who also claims also to have received a letter from Poirot that morning, accusing him of the murder of Barnabas Pandy...\n\nPoirot wonders how many more letters of this sort have been sent in his name. Who sent them, and why? More importantly, who is Barnabas Pandy, is he dead, and, if so, was he murdered?       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie">About Agatha Christie</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1589991473p3/123715.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie">Agatha Christie
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

followers
